### Post by hyperdude111 on 2009-10-31
Well it's not November where I am but it is for New Zealand and parts of Russia so I thought I'd make this thread

> Rules:

   1. Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
   2. If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
   3. Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
   4. The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
   5. The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
   6. Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
   7. To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

    Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
    Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
    Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
    Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-10-31
I GOT MY WOBBLY WINDOWS BACK!!! Woo-hoooo!

I've been a bit lonely without them since I switched to Crunchbang Lite, but I've switched now from Openbox to Compiz standalone, and I love it...It's all my eye-candy without clunky Gnome behind it :D

Anyway, here's what my desktop looks like now...

GTK: Espresso
Windows: Dark Roast Emerald Theme
Icons: Gnome Dust

Stock KDE wallpaper (I think?) and the same ol' Conky.

I'm also running Compiz-Deskmenu...I got used to the right-click menu in Openbox :)

Only thing I don't like is that it seems to be a bit buggy with Chromium...Sometimes it starts flashing randomly :S And why hasn't it got a shadow?!

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-11-01
> **bgreenaway said:**
> Really nice. What font is that? Love it.

Font is Petita Medium, available on dafont.com.

> **armageddon08 said:**
> Could I have your conkyrc ?

My .conkyrc:
```
# -- Conky settings -- #
background no
update_interval 1

cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2

override_utf8_locale yes

double_buffer yes
no_buffers yes

text_buffer_size 2048
imlib_cache_size 0

# -- Window specifications -- #

own_window yes
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below

border_inner_margin 0
border_outer_margin 0

minimum_size 1000 580
maximum_width 1000

alignment tl
gap_x 10
gap_y 10

# -- Graphics settings -- #
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no

# -- Text settings -- #
use_xft yes
xftfont Santana:size=12
xftalpha 0.8

uppercase no

default_color ffffff

# -- Lua Load -- #
lua_load ~/scripts/conky_widgets.lua
lua_draw_hook_pre widgets

TEXT
${goto 250}${voffset 20}${font Santana:size=36}${time %A, %d %B %Y}${font}
${goto 250}${voffset 25}${fs_bar 1,720 /}
${goto 870}${voffset 82}CPU ${cpu}%
${alignr 25}${voffset 82}MEM ${memperc}%
${goto 870}${voffset 82}FS ${fs_used_perc}%
${alignr 25}${voffset 82}BAT ${battery_percent BAT1}%
```

And my Conky Widgets script:
```
--[[
Conky Widgets by londonali1010 (2009)

This script is meant to be a "shell" to hold a suite of widgets for use in Conky.

To configure:
+ Copy the widget's code block (will be framed by --(( WIDGET NAME )) and --(( END WIDGET NAME )), with "[" instead of "(") somewhere between "require 'cairo'" and "function conky_widgets()", ensuring not to paste into another widget's code block
+ To call the widget, add the following just before the last "end" of the entire script:
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	NAME_OF_FUNCTION(cr, OPTIONS)
	cairo_destroy(cr)
+ Replace OPTIONS with the options for your widget (should be specified in the widget's code block) 

Call this script in Conky using the following before TEXT (assuming you save this script to ~/scripts/conky_widgets.lua):
	lua_load ~/scripts/conky_widgets.lua
	lua_draw_hook_pre widgets
	
Changelog:
+ v1.0 -- Original release (17.10.2009)
]]

require 'cairo'

--[[ AIR CLOCK WIDGET ]]
--[[ Options (xc, yc, size):
	"xc" and "yc" are the x and y coordinates of the centre of the clock, in pixels, relative to the top left of the Conky window
	"size" is the total size of the widget, in pixels ]]

function air_clock(cr, xc, yc, size)
	local offset = 0
	
	shadow_width = size * 0.03
	shadow_xoffset = 0
	shadow_yoffset = size * 0.01
	
	if shadow_xoffset >= shadow_yoffset then
		offset = shadow_xoffset
	else offset = shadow_yoffset
	end
	
	local clock_r = (size - 2 * offset) / (2 * 1.25)
		
	show_seconds=true
	
	-- Grab time
	
	local hours=os.date("%I")
	local mins=os.date("%M")
	local secs=os.date("%S")
	
	secs_arc=(2*math.pi/60)*secs
	mins_arc=(2*math.pi/60)*mins
	hours_arc=(2*math.pi/12)*hours+mins_arc/60
	
	-- Drop shadow
	
	local ds_pat=cairo_pattern_create_radial(xc+shadow_xoffset,yc+shadow_yoffset,clock_r*1.25,xc+shadow_xoffset,yc+shadow_yoffset,clock_r*1.25+shadow_width)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(ds_pat,0,0,0,0,0.2)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(ds_pat,1,0,0,0,0)
	
	cairo_move_to(cr,0,0)
	cairo_line_to(cr,conky_window.width,0)
	cairo_line_to(cr,conky_window.width, conky_window.height)
	cairo_line_to(cr,0,conky_window.height)
	cairo_close_path(cr)
	cairo_new_sub_path(cr)
	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,clock_r*1.25,0,2*math.pi)
	cairo_set_source(cr,ds_pat)
	cairo_set_fill_rule(cr,CAIRO_FILL_RULE_EVEN_ODD)
	cairo_fill(cr)
	
	-- Glassy border
	
	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,clock_r*1.25,0,2*math.pi)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,0.5,0.5,0.5,0.2)
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,1)
	cairo_stroke(cr)
	
	local border_pat=cairo_pattern_create_linear(xc,yc-clock_r*1.25,xc,yc+clock_r*1.25)
	
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(border_pat,0,1,1,1,0.7)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(border_pat,0.3,1,1,1,0)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(border_pat,0.5,1,1,1,0)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(border_pat,0.7,1,1,1,0)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(border_pat,1,1,1,1,0.7)
	cairo_set_source(cr,border_pat)
	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,clock_r*1.125,0,2*math.pi)
	cairo_close_path(cr)
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,clock_r*0.25)
	cairo_stroke(cr)
	
	-- Set clock face
	
	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,clock_r,0,2*math.pi)
	cairo_close_path(cr)
	
	local face_pat=cairo_pattern_create_radial(xc,yc-clock_r*0.75,0,xc,yc,clock_r)
	
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(face_pat,0,1,1,1,0.9)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(face_pat,0.5,1,1,1,0.9)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(face_pat,1,0.9,0.9,0.9,0.9)
	cairo_set_source(cr,face_pat)
	cairo_fill_preserve(cr)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,0.5,0.5,0.5,0.2)
	cairo_set_line_width(cr, 1)
	cairo_stroke (cr)
	
	-- Draw hour hand
	
	xh=xc+0.7*clock_r*math.sin(hours_arc)
	yh=yc-0.7*clock_r*math.cos(hours_arc)
	cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
	cairo_line_to(cr,xh,yh)
	
	cairo_set_line_cap(cr,CAIRO_LINE_CAP_ROUND)
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,5)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,0,0,0,0.5)
	cairo_stroke(cr)
	
	-- Draw minute hand
	
	xm=xc+0.9*clock_r*math.sin(mins_arc)
	ym=yc-0.9*clock_r*math.cos(mins_arc)
	cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
	cairo_line_to(cr,xm,ym)
	
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,3)
	cairo_stroke(cr)
	
	-- Draw seconds hand
	
	if show_seconds then
		xs=xc+0.9*clock_r*math.sin(secs_arc)
		ys=yc-0.9*clock_r*math.cos(secs_arc)
		cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
		cairo_line_to(cr,xs,ys)
	
		cairo_set_line_width(cr,1)
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	end
end

--[[ END AIR CLOCK WIDGET ]]

--[[ RING WIDGET ]]
--[[ Options (name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle):
	"name" is the type of stat to display; you can choose from 'cpu', 'memperc', 'fs_used_perc', 'battery_used_perc'.
	"arg" is the argument to the stat type, e.g. if in Conky you would write ${cpu cpu0}, 'cpu0' would be the argument. If you would not use an argument in the Conky variable, use ''.
	"max" is the maximum value of the ring. If the Conky variable outputs a percentage, use 100.
	"bg_colour" is the colour of the base ring.
	"bg_alpha" is the alpha value of the base ring.
	"fg_colour" is the colour of the indicator part of the ring.
	"fg_alpha" is the alpha value of the indicator part of the ring.
	"x" and "y" are the x and y coordinates of the centre of the ring, relative to the top left corner of the Conky window.
	"radius" is the radius of the ring.
	"thickness" is the thickness of the ring, centred around the radius.
	"start_angle" is the starting angle of the ring, in degrees, clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative.
	"end_angle" is the ending angle of the ring, in degrees, clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative, but must be larger (e.g. more clockwise) than start_angle. ]]

function ring(cr, name, arg, max, bgc, bga, fgc, fga, xc, yc, r, t, sa, ea)
	local function rgb_to_r_g_b(colour,alpha)
		return ((colour / 0x10000) % 0x100) / 255., ((colour / 0x100) % 0x100) / 255., (colour % 0x100) / 255., alpha
	end
	
	local function draw_ring(pct)
		local angle_0=sa*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
		local angle_f=ea*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
		local pct_arc=pct*(angle_f-angle_0)

		-- Draw background ring

		cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,r,angle_0,angle_f)
		cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(bgc,bga))
		cairo_set_line_width(cr,t)
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	
		-- Draw indicator ring

		cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,r,angle_0,angle_0+pct_arc)
		cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(fgc,fga))
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	end
	
	local function setup_ring()
		local str = ''
		local value = 0
		
		str = string.format('${%s %s}', name, arg)
		str = conky_parse(str)
		
		value = tonumber(str)
		if value == nil then value = 0 end
		pct = value/max
		
		draw_ring(pct)
	end	
	
	local updates=conky_parse('${updates}')
	update_num=tonumber(updates)
	
	if update_num>5 then setup_ring() end
end

--[[ END RING WIDGET ]]

--[[ RING (COUNTER-CLOCKWISE) WIDGET ]]
--[[ by londonali1010 (2009) ]]
--[[ Options (name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle):
	"name" is the type of stat to display; you can choose from 'cpu', 'memperc', 'fs_used_perc', 'battery_used_perc'.
	"arg" is the argument to the stat type, e.g. if in Conky you would write ${cpu cpu0}, 'cpu0' would be the argument. If you would not use an argument in the Conky variable, use ''.
	"max" is the maximum value of the ring. If the Conky variable outputs a percentage, use 100.
	"bg_colour" is the colour of the base ring.
	"bg_alpha" is the alpha value of the base ring.
	"fg_colour" is the colour of the indicator part of the ring.
	"fg_alpha" is the alpha value of the indicator part of the ring.
	"x" and "y" are the x and y coordinates of the centre of the ring, relative to the top left corner of the Conky window.
	"radius" is the radius of the ring.
	"thickness" is the thickness of the ring, centred around the radius.
	"start_angle" is the starting angle of the ring, in degrees, counter-clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative.
	"end_angle" is the ending angle of the ring, in degrees, counter-clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative, but must be larger (e.g. more counter-clockwise) than start_angle. ]]

function ring_ccw(cr, name, arg, max, bgc, bga, fgc, fga, xc, yc, r, t, sa, ea)
	local function rgb_to_r_g_b(colour,alpha)
		return ((colour / 0x10000) % 0x100) / 255., ((colour / 0x100) % 0x100) / 255., (colour % 0x100) / 255., alpha
	end
	
	local function draw_ring(pct)
		local angle_0=sa*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
		local angle_f=ea*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
		local pct_arc=pct*(angle_f-angle_0)

		-- Draw background ring

		cairo_arc_negative(cr,xc,yc,r,angle_0,angle_f)
		cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(bgc,bga))
		cairo_set_line_width(cr,t)
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	
		-- Draw indicator ring

		cairo_arc_negative(cr,xc,yc,r,angle_0,angle_0-pct_arc)
		cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(fgc,fga))
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	end
	
	local function setup_ring()
		local str = ''
		local value = 0
		
		str = string.format('${%s %s}', name, arg)
		str = conky_parse(str)
		
		value = tonumber(str)
		if value == nil then value = 0 end
		pct = value/max
		
		draw_ring(pct)
	end	
	
	local updates=conky_parse('${updates}')
	update_num=tonumber(updates)
	
	if update_num>5 then setup_ring() end
end

--[[ END RING (COUNTER-CLOCKWISE) WIDGET ]]

--[[ CLOCK HANDS WIDGET ]]
--[[ Options (xc, yc, colour, alpha, show_secs, size):
	"xc" and "yc" are the x and y coordinates of the centre of the clock hands, in pixels, relative to the top left corner of the Conky window
	"colour" is the colour of the clock hands, in OxFFFFFF formate
	"alpha" is the alpha of the hands, between 0 and 1
	"show_secs" is a boolean; set to true to show the seconds hand, otherwise set to false
	"size" is the total size of the widget (e.g. twice the length of the minutes hand), in pixels ]]

function clock_hands(cr, xc, yc, colour, alpha, show_secs, size)
	local function rgb_to_r_g_b(colour,alpha)
		return ((colour / 0x10000) % 0x100) / 255., ((colour / 0x100) % 0x100) / 255., (colour % 0x100) / 255., alpha
	end
	
	local secs,mins,hours,secs_arc,mins_arc,hours_arc
	local xh,yh,xm,ym,xs,ys

	secs=os.date("%S")
	mins=os.date("%M")
	hours=os.date("%I")

	secs_arc=(2*math.pi/60)*secs
	mins_arc=(2*math.pi/60)*mins+secs_arc/60
	hours_arc=(2*math.pi/12)*hours+mins_arc/12

	xh=xc+0.4*size*math.sin(hours_arc)
	yh=yc-0.4*size*math.cos(hours_arc)
	cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
	cairo_line_to(cr,xh,yh)

	cairo_set_line_cap(cr,CAIRO_LINE_CAP_ROUND)
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,5)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(colour,alpha))
	cairo_stroke(cr)

	xm=xc+0.5*size*math.sin(mins_arc)
	ym=yc-0.5*size*math.cos(mins_arc)
	cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
	cairo_line_to(cr,xm,ym)

	cairo_set_line_width(cr,3)
	cairo_stroke(cr)

	if show_secs then
		xs=xc+0.5*size*math.sin(secs_arc)
		ys=yc-0.5*size*math.cos(secs_arc)
		cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
		cairo_line_to(cr,xs,ys)

		cairo_set_line_width(cr,1)
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	end
end

--[[ END CLOCK HANDS WIDGET ]]

function conky_widgets()
	if conky_window == nil then return end
	local cs = cairo_xlib_surface_create(conky_window.display, conky_window.drawable, conky_window.visual, conky_window.width, conky_window.height)
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	clock_hands(cr, 110, 110, 0xFFFFFF, 1, false, 180)
	cairo_destroy(cr)
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	ring(cr, 'time', '%S', 60, 0xFFFFFF, 0.2, 0xFFFFFF, 0.8, 110, 110, 100, 10, 0, 360)
	cairo_destroy(cr)
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	ring_ccw(cr, 'cpu', 'CPU0', 100, 0xFFFFFF, 0.2, 0xFFFFFF, 0.8, 920, 200, 50, 10, 180, 360) -- options: name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, fg_colour, fg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle
	cairo_destroy(cr)
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	ring(cr, 'memperc', '', 100, 0xFFFFFF, 0.2, 0xFFFFFF, 0.8, 920, 300, 50, 10, 180, 360) -- options: name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, fg_colour, fg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle
	cairo_destroy(cr)	
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	ring_ccw(cr, 'fs_used_perc', '/', 100, 0xFFFFFF, 0.2, 0xFFFFFF, 0.8, 920, 400, 50, 10, 180, 360) -- options: name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, fg_colour, fg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle
	cairo_destroy(cr)
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	ring(cr, 'battery_percent', 'BAT1', 100, 0xFFFFFF, 0.2, 0xFFFFFF, 0.8, 920, 500, 50, 10, 180, 360) -- options: name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, fg_colour, fg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle
	cairo_destroy(cr)
end
```

HTH!

### Post by armageddon08 on 2009-11-01
> **londonali1010 said:**
> Font is Petita Medium, available on dafont.com.



My .conkyrc:
```
# -- Conky settings -- #
background no
update_interval 1

cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2

override_utf8_locale yes

double_buffer yes
no_buffers yes

text_buffer_size 2048
imlib_cache_size 0

# -- Window specifications -- #

own_window yes
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below

border_inner_margin 0
border_outer_margin 0

minimum_size 1000 580
maximum_width 1000

alignment tl
gap_x 10
gap_y 10

# -- Graphics settings -- #
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no

# -- Text settings -- #
use_xft yes
xftfont Santana:size=12
xftalpha 0.8

uppercase no

default_color ffffff

# -- Lua Load -- #
lua_load ~/scripts/conky_widgets.lua
lua_draw_hook_pre widgets

TEXT
${goto 250}${voffset 20}${font Santana:size=36}${time %A, %d %B %Y}${font}
${goto 250}${voffset 25}${fs_bar 1,720 /}
${goto 870}${voffset 82}CPU ${cpu}%
${alignr 25}${voffset 82}MEM ${memperc}%
${goto 870}${voffset 82}FS ${fs_used_perc}%
${alignr 25}${voffset 82}BAT ${battery_percent BAT1}%
```

And my Conky Widgets script:
```
--[[
Conky Widgets by londonali1010 (2009)

This script is meant to be a "shell" to hold a suite of widgets for use in Conky.

To configure:
+ Copy the widget's code block (will be framed by --(( WIDGET NAME )) and --(( END WIDGET NAME )), with "[" instead of "(") somewhere between "require 'cairo'" and "function conky_widgets()", ensuring not to paste into another widget's code block
+ To call the widget, add the following just before the last "end" of the entire script:
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	NAME_OF_FUNCTION(cr, OPTIONS)
	cairo_destroy(cr)
+ Replace OPTIONS with the options for your widget (should be specified in the widget's code block) 

Call this script in Conky using the following before TEXT (assuming you save this script to ~/scripts/conky_widgets.lua):
	lua_load ~/scripts/conky_widgets.lua
	lua_draw_hook_pre widgets
	
Changelog:
+ v1.0 -- Original release (17.10.2009)
]]

require 'cairo'

--[[ AIR CLOCK WIDGET ]]
--[[ Options (xc, yc, size):
	"xc" and "yc" are the x and y coordinates of the centre of the clock, in pixels, relative to the top left of the Conky window
	"size" is the total size of the widget, in pixels ]]

function air_clock(cr, xc, yc, size)
	local offset = 0
	
	shadow_width = size * 0.03
	shadow_xoffset = 0
	shadow_yoffset = size * 0.01
	
	if shadow_xoffset >= shadow_yoffset then
		offset = shadow_xoffset
	else offset = shadow_yoffset
	end
	
	local clock_r = (size - 2 * offset) / (2 * 1.25)
		
	show_seconds=true
	
	-- Grab time
	
	local hours=os.date("%I")
	local mins=os.date("%M")
	local secs=os.date("%S")
	
	secs_arc=(2*math.pi/60)*secs
	mins_arc=(2*math.pi/60)*mins
	hours_arc=(2*math.pi/12)*hours+mins_arc/60
	
	-- Drop shadow
	
	local ds_pat=cairo_pattern_create_radial(xc+shadow_xoffset,yc+shadow_yoffset,clock_r*1.25,xc+shadow_xoffset,yc+shadow_yoffset,clock_r*1.25+shadow_width)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(ds_pat,0,0,0,0,0.2)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(ds_pat,1,0,0,0,0)
	
	cairo_move_to(cr,0,0)
	cairo_line_to(cr,conky_window.width,0)
	cairo_line_to(cr,conky_window.width, conky_window.height)
	cairo_line_to(cr,0,conky_window.height)
	cairo_close_path(cr)
	cairo_new_sub_path(cr)
	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,clock_r*1.25,0,2*math.pi)
	cairo_set_source(cr,ds_pat)
	cairo_set_fill_rule(cr,CAIRO_FILL_RULE_EVEN_ODD)
	cairo_fill(cr)
	
	-- Glassy border
	
	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,clock_r*1.25,0,2*math.pi)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,0.5,0.5,0.5,0.2)
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,1)
	cairo_stroke(cr)
	
	local border_pat=cairo_pattern_create_linear(xc,yc-clock_r*1.25,xc,yc+clock_r*1.25)
	
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(border_pat,0,1,1,1,0.7)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(border_pat,0.3,1,1,1,0)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(border_pat,0.5,1,1,1,0)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(border_pat,0.7,1,1,1,0)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(border_pat,1,1,1,1,0.7)
	cairo_set_source(cr,border_pat)
	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,clock_r*1.125,0,2*math.pi)
	cairo_close_path(cr)
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,clock_r*0.25)
	cairo_stroke(cr)
	
	-- Set clock face
	
	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,clock_r,0,2*math.pi)
	cairo_close_path(cr)
	
	local face_pat=cairo_pattern_create_radial(xc,yc-clock_r*0.75,0,xc,yc,clock_r)
	
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(face_pat,0,1,1,1,0.9)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(face_pat,0.5,1,1,1,0.9)
	cairo_pattern_add_color_stop_rgba(face_pat,1,0.9,0.9,0.9,0.9)
	cairo_set_source(cr,face_pat)
	cairo_fill_preserve(cr)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,0.5,0.5,0.5,0.2)
	cairo_set_line_width(cr, 1)
	cairo_stroke (cr)
	
	-- Draw hour hand
	
	xh=xc+0.7*clock_r*math.sin(hours_arc)
	yh=yc-0.7*clock_r*math.cos(hours_arc)
	cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
	cairo_line_to(cr,xh,yh)
	
	cairo_set_line_cap(cr,CAIRO_LINE_CAP_ROUND)
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,5)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,0,0,0,0.5)
	cairo_stroke(cr)
	
	-- Draw minute hand
	
	xm=xc+0.9*clock_r*math.sin(mins_arc)
	ym=yc-0.9*clock_r*math.cos(mins_arc)
	cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
	cairo_line_to(cr,xm,ym)
	
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,3)
	cairo_stroke(cr)
	
	-- Draw seconds hand
	
	if show_seconds then
		xs=xc+0.9*clock_r*math.sin(secs_arc)
		ys=yc-0.9*clock_r*math.cos(secs_arc)
		cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
		cairo_line_to(cr,xs,ys)
	
		cairo_set_line_width(cr,1)
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	end
end

--[[ END AIR CLOCK WIDGET ]]

--[[ RING WIDGET ]]
--[[ Options (name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle):
	"name" is the type of stat to display; you can choose from 'cpu', 'memperc', 'fs_used_perc', 'battery_used_perc'.
	"arg" is the argument to the stat type, e.g. if in Conky you would write ${cpu cpu0}, 'cpu0' would be the argument. If you would not use an argument in the Conky variable, use ''.
	"max" is the maximum value of the ring. If the Conky variable outputs a percentage, use 100.
	"bg_colour" is the colour of the base ring.
	"bg_alpha" is the alpha value of the base ring.
	"fg_colour" is the colour of the indicator part of the ring.
	"fg_alpha" is the alpha value of the indicator part of the ring.
	"x" and "y" are the x and y coordinates of the centre of the ring, relative to the top left corner of the Conky window.
	"radius" is the radius of the ring.
	"thickness" is the thickness of the ring, centred around the radius.
	"start_angle" is the starting angle of the ring, in degrees, clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative.
	"end_angle" is the ending angle of the ring, in degrees, clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative, but must be larger (e.g. more clockwise) than start_angle. ]]

function ring(cr, name, arg, max, bgc, bga, fgc, fga, xc, yc, r, t, sa, ea)
	local function rgb_to_r_g_b(colour,alpha)
		return ((colour / 0x10000) % 0x100) / 255., ((colour / 0x100) % 0x100) / 255., (colour % 0x100) / 255., alpha
	end
	
	local function draw_ring(pct)
		local angle_0=sa*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
		local angle_f=ea*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
		local pct_arc=pct*(angle_f-angle_0)

		-- Draw background ring

		cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,r,angle_0,angle_f)
		cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(bgc,bga))
		cairo_set_line_width(cr,t)
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	
		-- Draw indicator ring

		cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,r,angle_0,angle_0+pct_arc)
		cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(fgc,fga))
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	end
	
	local function setup_ring()
		local str = ''
		local value = 0
		
		str = string.format('${%s %s}', name, arg)
		str = conky_parse(str)
		
		value = tonumber(str)
		if value == nil then value = 0 end
		pct = value/max
		
		draw_ring(pct)
	end	
	
	local updates=conky_parse('${updates}')
	update_num=tonumber(updates)
	
	if update_num>5 then setup_ring() end
end

--[[ END RING WIDGET ]]

--[[ RING (COUNTER-CLOCKWISE) WIDGET ]]
--[[ by londonali1010 (2009) ]]
--[[ Options (name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle):
	"name" is the type of stat to display; you can choose from 'cpu', 'memperc', 'fs_used_perc', 'battery_used_perc'.
	"arg" is the argument to the stat type, e.g. if in Conky you would write ${cpu cpu0}, 'cpu0' would be the argument. If you would not use an argument in the Conky variable, use ''.
	"max" is the maximum value of the ring. If the Conky variable outputs a percentage, use 100.
	"bg_colour" is the colour of the base ring.
	"bg_alpha" is the alpha value of the base ring.
	"fg_colour" is the colour of the indicator part of the ring.
	"fg_alpha" is the alpha value of the indicator part of the ring.
	"x" and "y" are the x and y coordinates of the centre of the ring, relative to the top left corner of the Conky window.
	"radius" is the radius of the ring.
	"thickness" is the thickness of the ring, centred around the radius.
	"start_angle" is the starting angle of the ring, in degrees, counter-clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative.
	"end_angle" is the ending angle of the ring, in degrees, counter-clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative, but must be larger (e.g. more counter-clockwise) than start_angle. ]]

function ring_ccw(cr, name, arg, max, bgc, bga, fgc, fga, xc, yc, r, t, sa, ea)
	local function rgb_to_r_g_b(colour,alpha)
		return ((colour / 0x10000) % 0x100) / 255., ((colour / 0x100) % 0x100) / 255., (colour % 0x100) / 255., alpha
	end
	
	local function draw_ring(pct)
		local angle_0=sa*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
		local angle_f=ea*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
		local pct_arc=pct*(angle_f-angle_0)

		-- Draw background ring

		cairo_arc_negative(cr,xc,yc,r,angle_0,angle_f)
		cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(bgc,bga))
		cairo_set_line_width(cr,t)
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	
		-- Draw indicator ring

		cairo_arc_negative(cr,xc,yc,r,angle_0,angle_0-pct_arc)
		cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(fgc,fga))
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	end
	
	local function setup_ring()
		local str = ''
		local value = 0
		
		str = string.format('${%s %s}', name, arg)
		str = conky_parse(str)
		
		value = tonumber(str)
		if value == nil then value = 0 end
		pct = value/max
		
		draw_ring(pct)
	end	
	
	local updates=conky_parse('${updates}')
	update_num=tonumber(updates)
	
	if update_num>5 then setup_ring() end
end

--[[ END RING (COUNTER-CLOCKWISE) WIDGET ]]

--[[ CLOCK HANDS WIDGET ]]
--[[ Options (xc, yc, colour, alpha, show_secs, size):
	"xc" and "yc" are the x and y coordinates of the centre of the clock hands, in pixels, relative to the top left corner of the Conky window
	"colour" is the colour of the clock hands, in OxFFFFFF formate
	"alpha" is the alpha of the hands, between 0 and 1
	"show_secs" is a boolean; set to true to show the seconds hand, otherwise set to false
	"size" is the total size of the widget (e.g. twice the length of the minutes hand), in pixels ]]

function clock_hands(cr, xc, yc, colour, alpha, show_secs, size)
	local function rgb_to_r_g_b(colour,alpha)
		return ((colour / 0x10000) % 0x100) / 255., ((colour / 0x100) % 0x100) / 255., (colour % 0x100) / 255., alpha
	end
	
	local secs,mins,hours,secs_arc,mins_arc,hours_arc
	local xh,yh,xm,ym,xs,ys

	secs=os.date("%S")
	mins=os.date("%M")
	hours=os.date("%I")

	secs_arc=(2*math.pi/60)*secs
	mins_arc=(2*math.pi/60)*mins+secs_arc/60
	hours_arc=(2*math.pi/12)*hours+mins_arc/12

	xh=xc+0.4*size*math.sin(hours_arc)
	yh=yc-0.4*size*math.cos(hours_arc)
	cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
	cairo_line_to(cr,xh,yh)

	cairo_set_line_cap(cr,CAIRO_LINE_CAP_ROUND)
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,5)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(colour,alpha))
	cairo_stroke(cr)

	xm=xc+0.5*size*math.sin(mins_arc)
	ym=yc-0.5*size*math.cos(mins_arc)
	cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
	cairo_line_to(cr,xm,ym)

	cairo_set_line_width(cr,3)
	cairo_stroke(cr)

	if show_secs then
		xs=xc+0.5*size*math.sin(secs_arc)
		ys=yc-0.5*size*math.cos(secs_arc)
		cairo_move_to(cr,xc,yc)
		cairo_line_to(cr,xs,ys)

		cairo_set_line_width(cr,1)
		cairo_stroke(cr)
	end
end

--[[ END CLOCK HANDS WIDGET ]]

function conky_widgets()
	if conky_window == nil then return end
	local cs = cairo_xlib_surface_create(conky_window.display, conky_window.drawable, conky_window.visual, conky_window.width, conky_window.height)
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	clock_hands(cr, 110, 110, 0xFFFFFF, 1, false, 180)
	cairo_destroy(cr)
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	ring(cr, 'time', '%S', 60, 0xFFFFFF, 0.2, 0xFFFFFF, 0.8, 110, 110, 100, 10, 0, 360)
	cairo_destroy(cr)
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	ring_ccw(cr, 'cpu', 'CPU0', 100, 0xFFFFFF, 0.2, 0xFFFFFF, 0.8, 920, 200, 50, 10, 180, 360) -- options: name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, fg_colour, fg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle
	cairo_destroy(cr)
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	ring(cr, 'memperc', '', 100, 0xFFFFFF, 0.2, 0xFFFFFF, 0.8, 920, 300, 50, 10, 180, 360) -- options: name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, fg_colour, fg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle
	cairo_destroy(cr)	
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	ring_ccw(cr, 'fs_used_perc', '/', 100, 0xFFFFFF, 0.2, 0xFFFFFF, 0.8, 920, 400, 50, 10, 180, 360) -- options: name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, fg_colour, fg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle
	cairo_destroy(cr)
	
	cr = cairo_create(cs)
	ring(cr, 'battery_percent', 'BAT1', 100, 0xFFFFFF, 0.2, 0xFFFFFF, 0.8, 920, 500, 50, 10, 180, 360) -- options: name, arg, max, bg_colour, bg_alpha, fg_colour, fg_alpha, xc, yc, radius, thickness, start_angle, end_angle
	cairo_destroy(cr)
end
```

HTH!

Thank you very much. :D

### Post by Amstell on 2009-11-01
> **quickdraw said:**
> VERY impressive on the conky information. I'd love to be able to get that good with scripts and stuff.

Pretty simple actually.
```

TEXT
${voffset 10}${font Route 3:size=64}${time %k}${font} ${offset -2}${voffset -56}${font Route 3:size=48}${time %M}${font}${offset -70}${voffset 18}${time %A}, ${time %d} ${time %b} ${time %Y}
${execi 1000 tide -l "San Diego" > /home/woody/tides.txt}
${voffset 10}${execi 1000 head /home/woody/tides.txt}

:: Mission Beach Buoy - Station 46231 ::

${execi 1000 curl  http://www.ndbc.noaa.gov/data/latest_obs/46231.rss | sed -e :a -e 's/<[^>]*>//g;/</N' | sed -e 's/[ \t]*//' | sed -e '/^ *$/d' | sed -n 17,20p | sed -e 's/°//g' > /home/woody/swell.txt}
${execi 1000 cat /home/woody/swell.txt}

:: Torrey Pines Outer Buoy - Station 46225 ::
${execi 1000 curl  http://www.ndbc.noaa.gov/data/latest_obs/46225.rss | sed -e :a -e 's/<[^>]*>//g;/</N' | sed -e 's/[ \t]*//' | sed -e '/^ *$/d' | sed -n 17,20p | sed -e 's/°//g' > /home/woody/swell2.txt}
${execi 1000 cat /home/woody/swell2.txt}

:: Oceanside Offshore - Station 46224 ::
${execi 1000 curl  http://www.ndbc.noaa.gov/data/latest_obs/46224.rss | sed -e :a -e 's/<[^>]*>//g;/</N' | sed -e 's/[ \t]*//' | sed -e '/^ *$/d' | sed -n 17,20p | sed -e 's/°//g' > /home/woody/swell2.txt}
${execi 1000 cat /home/woody/swell2.txt}

${execi 1000 wget http://www.lajollasurf.org/images/pacpanimne.gif -O /home/woody/wave.gif}${voffset 600}${image /home/woody/wave.gif -p 10,700 -s 500x450}

```

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-11-03
> **liquidbee said:**
> Is that tint2 ? Also, how can I make my terminal look like yours ( I mean, no borders or title bar ) ?
tint2 it is.

I have this in my rc.xml (right above </ applications> )
```

    <application class="XTerm">
      <decor>no</decor>
    </application>

```

You also need to retain the border on undecorated windows (this is around line 50 in the default rc.xml):
```

    <keepBorder>yes</keepBorder>

```

---

### Post by the8thstar on 2009-11-07
Since I'm using both Gnome and KDE, here are my two desktops and their respective specs:

[COLOR="Green"]**Gnome**[/COLOR]

Icons : Hydroxygen
Gtk and Metacity : Plastique
Font: Sans 8

In /home/{yourusernamehere}/.themes/Plastique/gtk-2.0, I manually modified gtkrc and panel.rc files to allow for my font to be displayed correctly.

[B][COLOR="Blue"]
KDE[/COLOR][/B]

Icons : Hydroxygen
KDE styles : Oxygen
Font : Dejavu Sans 7

The background is the same on both environments : 115028-vladstudio_bug_1600x1200.jpg found on kde-look.org.

Obviously, these themes look very close. This was done for the sake of consistency. The thumbnails don't do justice to the simplicity and beauty of these compositions.

Enjoy.

Can't you just compile it?
> **Aspergillus said:**
> WOWWWW!!!!

details please?
Thanks. Other than what's listed above, I'm using Bespin for the widgets and window decorations, Oxygen refit black for my icons, and Cream for the plasma theme.

> **londonali1010 said:**
> I GOTTA get me some of that sideways titlebar action!!!
I really like it.


Also, if anyone's interested, I've written a small shell function that uploads images to omploader.org and spits back the relevant links. This is what it looks like:
[IMG]http://omploader.org/vMnB2eQ[/IMG]
And here's the code (meant to go in .bashrc):
[PHP]ompload() { curl -F file1=@"$1" http://omploader.org/upload|awk '/class="upload"/{for(i=1;i<7;i++){getline;if(i!=5&&i!=3){gsub(/<[^<]*?\/?>/,"");$1=$1;sub(/^/,"\033[0;34m");sub(/:/,"\033[0m:");print}}}';}[/PHP]

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-11-07
> **vagrantrooper said:**
> How do you have the drop shadow on the digi clock?

It's the adjustable clock plasmoid. It allows formatting with html and supports webkit css extensions. This is the code that I'm using:
[HTML]<div style="text-align: center;color:#eee; white-space: pre; margin-top:0px; margin-right: 5px; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-left: 0px; -webkit-box-reflect: below -10px -webkit-gradient(linear, 0% 0%, 0% 100%, from(transparent), color-stop(0.5, black), to(white)) 0 0 0 0 stretch stretch; "><span style="font-family:'Y2K Neophyte';font-size: large;">%l</span><span style="font-family:'Y2K Neophyte';font-size: medium;">%M</span></div>[/HTML]

---

### Post by emigrant on 2009-11-07
> **eightmillion said:**
> 

Also, if anyone's interested, I've written a small shell function that uploads images to omploader.org and spits back the relevant links.

man would you mind sharing the bash script? :KS

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-11-07
> **emigrant said:**
> man would you mind sharing the bash script? :KS

It's in the post at the bottom, but here it is again:

[PHP]ompload() { curl -F file1=@"$1" http://omploader.org/upload|awk '/class="upload"/{for(i=1;i<7;i++){getline;if(i!=5&&i!=3){gsub(/<[^<]*?\/?>/,"");$1=$1;sub(/^/,"\033[0;34m");sub(/:/,"\033[0m:");print}}}';} [/PHP]

Just put it in your ~/.bashrc file and you'll be good to go. (If you want to use it right away, you'll have to source you bashrc with the command: "source .bashrc")

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-11-07
> **eightmillion said:**
> It's in the post at the bottom, but here it is again:

[php]ompload() { curl -F file1=@"$1" http://omploader.org/upload|awk '/class="upload"/{for(i=1;i<7;i++){getline;if(i!=5&&i!=3){gsub(/<[^<]*?\/?>/,"");$1=$1;sub(/^/,"\033[0;34m");sub(/:/,"\033[0m:");print}}}';} [/php]Just put it in your ~/.bashrc file and you'll be good to go. (If you want to use it right away, you'll have to source you bashrc with the command: "source .bashrc")
Gotta love that syntax highlighting ;)

> **Hund said:**
> [[IMG]http://th03.deviantart.net/fs51/300W/f/2009/311/d/4/d4dd7b7a114ea872b155c4c307cb0241.png[/IMG]]("http://ebupof.deviantart.com/art/My-Desktop-November-2009-142814623")

Info in the screenshot.

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-11-08
> **h!v said:**
> Details would be? Fonts in Conky especially.

The fonts in the conky are "Sketch Block" for the clock, "Santana" for the headers, and "cure" for the main text. Sketch Block and Santana are on dafont, cure is part of artwiz's font package, you can google it for more info.
The obtheme is a mod of arch.blue, gtk is elegant for rent, icons are allgrey, wallpaper is darkwood, and all can be found with a simple google search! :)

---

### Post by MaxIBoy on 2009-11-09
I've had the same GTK theme on this laptop for a while, but I just now did a lot of customization on the gnome panel:

[LIST]
[*]Replace the GNOME menu bar with custom menus. Places menu needed to be recreated from scratch but I was able to get rid of all its features that I didn't need.
[*]Created custom icons for each one (instead of just a single icon for Applications.) The text labels and gradient backgrounds are all part of the icons and were made from screenshots of my old menu bar.
[*]Add "Office" menu to the panel with yet another such custom icon (plan to do the same for Graphics.)
[*]Use gnome_swallow applet to embed Audacious2 in the panel (FINALLY! I'd been looking for a way to do this for ages!) I plan to write a script to handle launching it/dealing with a preexisting instance, so I can associate sound files with this.
[/LIST]

### Post by TakezoB on 2009-11-09
Hey did you see that docky and gnome-do split!
In karmic you already have docky in the repos. And i prefer an independant docky for two reasons:
-you can put it on the left or right side of the screen
-gnome-do seems useless with gnome-shell(wich I use)
Now here is my desktop. Nothing special.

Ps: and docky come with a lot of other improvement like themes. Here is an article wich explain it, very usefull: [http://www.webupd8.org/2009/10/install-docky-and-update-gnome-shell.html](http://www.webupd8.org/2009/10/install-docky-and-update-gnome-shell.html)

### Post by koleoptero on 2009-11-10
So, I tried staying in Kubuntu for 2 days, and realized that it's a very modern and nice environment, with very good programs (I just love k3b) and lots of bling. BUT it's still a little rough around the edges (let's face it, it's not that long in development for a DE, it needs some more) and it's too heavy for my machine. The latter reason being the most important, I switched back to gnome.

I got in a frenzy of customization today, and I really like the way things worked out. Conky took a while to get to the proper shape (couldn't fit as it was in the dark space down below with this wallpaper) but a HUGE **thank you **to londonali for putting the instructions on top of the script and making it so easy to understand, great job!

So, for now, I've gone dark. :D

EDIT: I see photobucket doesn't show them in 100% size. Anyone knows why?

### Post by koleoptero on 2009-11-11
> **pwnst*r said:**
> exACTLY how i feel, down to K3B.  i want details on your ff colours/skin if you care to share.
Firefox theme is foxdie graphite. It's my all time favourite, I rarely change it. It has various settings that you can change from a menu by clicking on the icon in the statusbar. My particular settings are:
Buttons: Muku 1
Layout: Firedark
Right X for the tabs
Apple logo in the misc settings.

This is the only theme that can fit (by changing settings) almost any desktop theme. All my previous screenshots were taken with this firefox theme.

### Post by The Real Dave on 2009-11-12
Anyone know if I can get the Humanity icons from Karmic for Jaunty? I love them, they're beautiful :) But Karmic, I love not so much :) I'd post my desktop but not much has changed, though, I feel like installing Kubunutu or openSUSE, I wanna try out KDE, but I don't want the 200Mb DL for the package ;)

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-11-12
> **The Real Dave said:**
> Anyone know if I can get the Humanity icons from Karmic for Jaunty? I love them, they're beautiful :) But Karmic, I love not so much :) I'd post my desktop but not much has changed, though, I feel like installing Kubunutu or openSUSE, I wanna try out KDE, but I don't want the 200Mb DL for the package ;)
You can just install the [karmic package]("https://launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/humanity-icon-theme/0.3.1-0ubuntu3/+build/1259903") in Jaunty, or, if you're wary of that, you can extract the deb file with "dpkg -x humanity-icon-theme_0.3.1-0ubuntu3_all.deb ." and then move the resulting folder "usr/share/icons/Humanity" to "/usr/share/icons/".

---

### Post by The Real Dave on 2009-11-12
> **eightmillion said:**
> You can just install the [karmic package]("https://launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/humanity-icon-theme/0.3.1-0ubuntu3/+build/1259903") in Jaunty, or, if you're wary of that, you can extract the deb file with "dpkg -x humanity-icon-theme_0.3.1-0ubuntu3_all.deb ." and then move the resulting folder "usr/share/icons/Humanity" to "/usr/share/icons/".

Thank you! :)

### Post by coldReactive on 2009-11-14

Sadly, pidgin causes the ugly look to still stay if I set the panel to transparent. :( I also can't see my network or volume icons very well.

---

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-11-14
> **coldReactive said:**
> Sadly, pidgin causes the ugly look to still stay if I set the panel to transparent. :( I also can't see my network or volume icons very well.

That's because you're just lowering the Opacity.

You have two choices.

1. Use a RGBA compatible theme. (This makes your theme transparent, with out making the content transparent (text, icons, etc.)

2. Just select a color for your panel background, and lower the opacity of it. (This will make your content on your panel still 100% visible, just with a transparent panel background)

---

### Post by vagrantrooper on 2009-11-14
> **coldReactive said:**
> Sadly, pidgin causes the ugly look to still stay if I set the panel to transparent. :( I also can't see my network or volume icons very well.


Heve you tried setting the panel transparency through compiz?

[Opacity, Brightness and Saturation]

In the Opacity tab select new and name it

type=dock

set opacity level to 89

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-11-15
> **JECHO said:**
> details???

And while you're at it, a larger shot wouldn't hurt, either.


First shot of the month. Might as well make it particularly self-indulgent.

Busy:
[[IMG]http://img121.imageshack.us/img121/7969/12400864.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img121.imageshack.us/img121/7969/12400864.jpg)
Somewhat recent versions of GTK/Emerald themes are in my sig. Mostly Mac fonts. Window resizing and placement made easy thanks to wmctrl shell scripts, bound to keyboard shortcuts. Also using compiz edge resistance.

Expo:
[[IMG]http://img5.imageshack.us/img5/7099/16060175.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img5.imageshack.us/img5/7099/16060175.jpg)
Hint of red to match the colour of my physical monitor. Accessible via mouse's 'forwards' button.

Clean:
[[IMG]http://img121.imageshack.us/img121/9908/94593539.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img121.imageshack.us/img121/9908/94593539.jpg)
Wall found somewhere on wallbase.net. Notes possible thanks to xpad, conky RSS and stats are in my sig. I make heavy use of compiz's 'workspace wheel'; scrolling over the desktop to change workspace. Unfortunately, due to some weird Gtk bug, it often happens, when it shouldn't.

Alt-tabbing:
[[IMG]http://img195.imageshack.us/img195/8893/58141892.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img195.imageshack.us/img195/8893/58141892.jpg)
Again, a hint of red. It's not so much that I like the 'cover flow' switcher, as it is that I dislike every other window switcher. Can also super/meta/windows key-tab to make it workspace-specific.

Scale:
[[IMG]http://img4.imageshack.us/img4/8214/16667561.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img4.imageshack.us/img4/8214/16667561.jpg)
Accessible via mouse's 'back' button. super/meta/windows key-'back', to make it workspace specific. Right-click to 'drag window to current workspace'. Middle-click to close window/crash compiz. Not that anyone cares, but I figured it best not to reveal client information, or all the email addresses I use.

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2009-11-16
Does someone know how to create a symbolic link between /usr/share/themes and ~/.themes ? cause I'm tired of seeing all gksudo started applications look like sh*t.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-11-16
```
sudo ln -s /path/to/your/user/account/themes/folder /root/.themes/
```

I personally just copy the themes I actually use to the root themes folder. That way, I can mod the colours of applications running as root.

Edit: Note the scrollbar colour.

[img]http://img22.imageshack.us/img22/4582/rootk.jpg[/img]

---

### Post by zagz on 2009-11-16

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-11-16
> **zagz said:**
> Then you know very little of Linux, and in fact Linux window transparency lets the user set opacity level, does Microsoft let the user do that?

1. The discussion is about *inner-window* transparency, not full transparency.  Inner-window transparency allows the user to make the background of a window transparent without lowering the opacity of the window's text or widgets (buttons, checkboxes, pull-down menus, etc.).  Reducing a window's opacity simply makes everything more transparent.

2. It is not a feature of Linux itself that provides window transparency.  You typically need to use a compositing window manager, such as Compiz in order to make a window truly transparent.

3. No, Microsoft does not give the user that ability as a feature of Windows.  You need to use a third-party application in order to do that.  However, as said above you need something like Compiz to create the effect in Linux.  Compiz is not a feature of Linux; it's a third-party application that tends to be favored by some distributions and is installed by default and included in their repositories.

---

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2009-11-16

However, as said above you need something like Compiz to create the effect in Linux.  **Compiz is not a feature of Linux; it's a third-party application **that tends to be favored by some distributions and is installed by default and included in their repositories.

Um... NOTHING is a feature of Linux. Linux is a kernel. Absolutely everything is a "third-party application".

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-11-16
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> Right but...  NOTHING is a "feature of Linux". It's just a platform. Panels aren't a feature of Linux. Window management isn't a feature of Linux. Icons aren't a feature of Linux. Linux is simply a kernel upon which tons of distros are built.

I understand that.  However, the person I was quoting did *not* seem to understand that.  He stated that window transparency was a feature of Linux.

> When you say Compiz isn't a "feature" of Linux, that's a little absurd because Linux has no features. There is no Linux "the operating system". Which one do you mean? Debian? Ubuntu? Fedora? Arch? Slack?

I know it sounds absurd, because I suppose I wasn't elaborate enough in my explanation or I did not word it correctly.  What I meant to say was that window transparency is not a feature of Linux, but a feature of Compiz, which itself is also not a feature of Linux or Linux-based operating systems (GNU/Linux, or what I really meant when I said "Linux as an operating system").

I was trying to compare the capabilities of two operating systems, Linux-based operating systems and Windows.  The person I was quoting claimed that Microsoft does not give the user the ability of changing the opacity of windows.  That is true; however, there are third-party applications that allow the user to do so.

Likewise, Linux-based operating systems (Ubuntu, Fedora, SUSE, Arch, etc.) do not *themselves* give users the ability of changing the opacity of windows.  Unlike Microsoft, however, many of them provide a third-party application (i.e. Compiz) that can.

[B]**OFF TOPIC OPINION**
[/B]
Either way, I personally wouldn't use an opacity changing program. What's the point? It just makes things harder to read because the content gets effected by it too. At least with something like Windows Aero, the transparency only effects the window frame and the content remains the same. Text is also highlighted with a white glow (that so many Linux users hate for some reason) to allow the user to read the text no matter what background you're using.

****OFF TOPIC OPINION****

---

### Post by AlexR1 on 2009-11-16
> **Islington said:**
> Impressive. Details?

I am running Ubuntu 9.10 (code name karmic koala).
Gtk / Metacity theme are pixmap, called Elegance 2.0 by me, available at [www.gnome-look.org](www.gnome-look.org), version I am running at the moment is a little bit different. 
Icon theme is Eikon,  I replaced folders with Kasual folders, and I am replacing some toher icons with Token light.
At the bottom custom panel with my favorites menu and on the side are rainlendar2 widgets, calendar to-do list clock and weather, good thing about rainlendar is I can use calendar from one theme and other widgets from another theme.Art work is rhythmbox  extension or addon.
Opacity of the nautilus and rhytmbox also opacity of the panel i can change by pressing alt key and scrolling mouse wheel,until i get desired effect.( I think this is thanks to Compiz ) since my theme do not use murrine engine.
I think I covered all, if you have more questions do not hesitate to contact me.

### Post by rjmdomingo2003 on 2009-11-17
> **londonali1010 said:**
> Have you tried Compiz standalone on Crunchbang? That's what I use, and I don't have any Conky issues with compositing...
I am using Compiz (stand-alone) but am having an issue with conky which is surrounded by a "shadow". Hook me up (PM?) with your .conkyrc &/or setting to remove this. Thanks.

---

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-11-17
> **rjmdomingo2003 said:**
> I am using Compiz (stand-alone) but am having an issue with conky which is surrounded by a "shadow". Hook me up (PM?) with your .conkyrc &/or setting to remove this. Thanks.

If your own_window_type is yes, you should be able to get rid of it by adding ```
&!(class=conky)
```to the shadow entry box under Window Decorations in CCSM. If that doesn't work, you can actually turn off shadows in CCSM altogether and just add them in for elements you want...Your Emerald theme will probably already have shadows for most windows, so you don't need that, then you can add in for panels (type=dock) and menus (type=menu, I think).

HTH.

---

> **Aspergillus said:**
> beautiful desktop...

may i make you a question...

how do you get the minimized applications in the panel as only icons without the text?

Icons and theme are pretty standard stuff. Had to edit the values of the bluetooth and volume systray icons to get a uniform look. Undecorated the windows because that's how I usually stick them when doing work.
[[IMG]http://img156.imageshack.us/img156/8800/200911230542561024x600s.png[/IMG]]("http://omploader.org/vMnUzdg")

Cheers~

### Post by chinmaya_n on 2009-11-23

System > Administration > Users and Groups !!
go there and unlock and select Properties of your username and change the REal name overthere !
Thats all !:popcorn:

If you want any changes to your system category wise ..... you can see here ***gnome-control-center***

### Post by gutterslob on 2009-11-23
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> 
Impressive. The font choice is a little odd, though. It invokes imagery of 3rd world dictatorships, littered with technicolour buildings and 'inspirational' propaganda.
Well, the font is called Bauhaus Medium and the wallpaper is Bauhausian-esque in its composition.
...and yes, it does have a somewhat "controversial" history. I could write an entire essay on this if you want, but I think the _[wiki]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bauhaus")_ link should give you the gist of it (it's not entirely accurate, though)
Ironically, the Nazi regime heavily criticised the Bauhaus school/movement, but used (unknowingly) some Bauhaus themes/influences in their propaganda/architecture/attire/etc.

Food for thought, and a highly off-topic post.
My apologies.

### Post by agas on 2009-11-23
icon:
This icon theme is a compilation of a few icon themes and a few sparse icons
found on [www.deviantart.com](www.deviantart.com) and [www.kde-look.org](www.kde-look.org). It is by no means complete
but hopefully (in time) it will be. The theme is based on the  reflection icon set by styrizo ([http://styrizo.deviantart.com](http://styrizo.deviantart.com)) and has
been enhanced with the minimal
perception set
by mandarancio
([http://mandarancio.deviantart.com/art/Minimal-perception-67892707](http://mandarancio.deviantart.com/art/Minimal-perception-67892707))
,the Black and White icon theme by carpelinx
([http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/black+++white+icons?content=24645](http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/black+++white+icons?content=24645)).
and the ecqlipse icon set by [http://chrfb.deviantart.com/](http://chrfb.deviantart.com/).

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-11-24
Finally found a notification daemon that doesn't look like crap and doesn't annoy me.

[url=http://img691.imageshack.us/img691/5808/screenshotag.jpg][img]http://img260.imageshack.us/img260/1979/screenshotsml.jpg[/img]
http://img691.imageshack.us/img691/5808/screenshotag.jpg[/url]

Xfce4-notifyd:
- can embed GTK+ widgets.
- can be themed.
- clicking on any normal part of it makes it go away; it doesn't focus the responsible application.
- can be configured in a basic manner (like, I dunno, *being able to choose the corner of the screen it pops up in*).
- you have some level of interaction/control, as opposed to notifications do whatever they feel like doing (*cough* - notify-osd).

---

Xfce4-notifyd:
- can embed GTK+ widgets.
- can be themed.
- clicking on any normal part of it makes it go away; it doesn't focus the responsible application.
- can be configured in a basic manner (like, I dunno, *being able to choose the corner of the screen it pops up in*).
- you have some level of interaction/control, as opposed to notifications do whatever they feel like doing (*cough* - notify-osd).

That's just the standard workspace switcher, with labels enabled. Can be done in Xfce 4.6 and the last two releases of Gnome.

Edit: RSS is my rather hacky conky config. See the link in my sig, for details. If you don't have the Mac fonts installed, use the one labelled, "generic".

### Post by mrdiego on 2009-11-25
> **MiCK.ca said:**
> how did mr. diego split the panes in Nautilus?

It's not a fake ... try it out ;)

> $ sudo add-apt-repository ppa:berndth/ppa
$ sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get upgrade
$ nautilus -q && nautilus &
$ exit

(Karmic)

With "F3" you get the second pane. Again "F3"... all as usual.

> **BDNiner said:**

I have installed awn from their ppa, not from the original repos. If you have too then go to the settings and change the mode to floaty. :) Then there's a slider at the bottom, I believe you can adjust how far away from the bottom you want it to be (not from the sides unfortunately :/)

C:\Windows\Resources\Themes\X2\Wallpapers

The wallpaper isn't hardwired into the theme, it's just in a folder that was placed within the theme folder.
